dou chastrement	with strengthening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	I know that strengthenings are customary in our law, and therefore I prefer not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to do so for .ij. reasons: one is that the mirrors respond when asked, and in strengthening the cure; and another, because we often need strengthening from certain beasts to aid us, such as goat and sheep and deer and other beasts. I say therefore that strengthenings are made according to .ij. methods: either by attraction or by fendingure. In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water, so that the joint becomes softened and flexible; then take it with your hand, so that it is reset and you no longer feel it. For strengthening of a cut: it is necessary to hold the beast, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then suspend it, and cover each opening with a .i. cap, when you have well cleansed them; and leave no small part of the subtle fascia that is beneath the veins; and this method of strengthening is more effective than that done by attraction, because in attraction something often remains by chance among the joints, whereby the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of the hemorrhoids
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds in men: one is when they occur between the thighs as if figured by nature in a woman's shape, where there are hairs, and sometimes it affects urination.  And the other way is in women, and they appear on the buttock like a rod with two thighs.  And the cure for men and women is to cauterize all the affected flesh, and to treat them as other wounds; in the second case, of those whose urine passes through the skin of the thighs, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenderness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenderness is an affected flesh on the natural part, so much that it is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the cure. It is necessary that you remove the superfluousness of the tenderness with your hand or with onions, and lightly touch; and do not push too hard in front, lest the blood come forth, then the cure of another wound as long as it is healthy; and there is another wound that grows at the mouth of the anus, and the embossing, and by chance it breaks out, and it has the appearance of a cow, and for this reason the ancient ones called it "cow disease". If you touch it, if we have said about the tenderness, and the cure as long as it is healthy.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pertus is small; and it is born naturally, or occurs by accident through disease that comes to be; or it is by chance adjustment, or subtle dou syfac, and is made in the marrow, or in the sides, or below, or wherever; and they hinder conception, and childbirth, and by chance the flowers have to be had; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the baile.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are overgrowths of veins which without proper treatment become accustomed, and when hemorrhoids become old they become thelul; and we have already said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will tell you those that receive curation. I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are deeply rooted in the marrow, and do not appear to the sense, it is not a cure by iron. Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, one can feel, are those that can be cured. It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then apply the altaelul as poultices, and the cope with its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the blood flows out, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galen, and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and confit with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back. And if it is inflamed, that's good. If not, then apply ventouses to the back and massage with iron; then take wine, and mix it with plantain juice or aglentier juice with old wine, and apply to the affected area. And when the abscess ripens, then cure the affected area thoroughly until it is healthy; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough chief, then it is necessary to cover as I said about thelul; and then cure until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Here is the translation:
de l’enfantement	of the birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The expert is first to recognize the figure of natural birth, and the signs are when you see the woman approach below, and desire to smell the air: then hasten the infants to come out quickly; then know that this birth is according to natural figure, and it issues from its chief, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, then you must press gently on her belly, so that the infant comes out quickly; for when it descends upon its chief, then is the second with him, and is removed the superfluous matter by good moderation; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes to the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or above, and is converted by an adventure on its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the expert to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out naturally upon its chief, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the virtues of it are weak, then make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and arise from the nature of oil or fenugreek being cooked, and then place the expert between her two small spatulas, which is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and find the second, and cut to its nail as much as the moisture which is in the cord was; and take hold of the woman's belly so that the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then you must clusterize the woman with musculating fenugreek oil; then make her take a drink and be consoled, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the infant is born. And if the hands issue forth, then you must gently press them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet high; then remove the seat from the ground, and hold onto the woman, so that she does not fall; and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant dies, then take hold of the hands at the counter which is placed before, and extract the infant, and gently press.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes onto its feet, if it needs to be held upright.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take hold of the feet and stretch them out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just as a knee, if you command to bend, and make it stretch with conditions;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps fiercely, then God wants.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump fiercely as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, take a poultice of hot water, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush everything in a mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the nature of the woman within and remove this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in a warm bath until beneath the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened beneath, have her a girdle of myrrh, and put it beneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make them sit on the seat, then make them lean back and hold their mouth and nose, and take hold of their belly lightly, because the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the escape of the child upon his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, if I put the basin under his hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be supported on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and be lying on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and he places his hands little by little, and then he takes the hands on the belly, and he lifts the cushions from below, until it is prepared downwards;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if he cannot jump, he takes his feet and moves them strongly, then he moves the belly upwards, then he puts out his hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and rock the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold herself back as much as the child is held.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	One must know how to reset the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot reset it, then make the woman lift up and go;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on a bed, and let her legs be straightened out;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then treat the muscle strain that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and it does not inflame, if it makes it sit on the seat, then studies to guide the hand back;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to natural posture, and make it stretch, and command that it take hold as far as the veins issue forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I think that you should hold its hand, then turn it little by little, and rock it gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then place on the natural muscle tone of the thigh and oil, as we have said, then instruct him to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make him sit on the seat, and instruct him to take hold; and make him steady.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for the entire second one
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner for the entire second one, then cut the second one at your finger, so that the moisture is evacuated.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and he should place his face on it and on his neck, if the cup of the poultice, so that it is not retained, and kills the infants;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it so that it fits, and instruct the woman to take care not to slip even once:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will be easier to straighten afterwards.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the dislocation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes not at all; it is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	They are strange things, and do not live much, if they do not receive a name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that, in order to be multiplied, and are divided by the syllable which is linked to the throat;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and no time do they issue naturally like all those below, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue grievously, thus the treatment as we have said, and let the subtle vein be treated, and make it whole and light, whatever it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as he values his health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	No times are formed in the marrow, i.e. one or two or three or four or five, or six, or seven, or up to fifteen, and all are fully formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is believed that the wise one knows all this, for it seems that chance brings similar things to him.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Do thus according to what is suitable.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman who has had a dead child or a miscarriage, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained by hand work;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is suitable that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has not had an accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be leaning on her back, and her knees bent downwards, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife holds the sheet of birth, or she is tied to the bed so that she does not fall during the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils of altaea and fenugreek, and sow flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and musk-like substances;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then gently wash the mother's legs, then she wants her to bend or she washes the ankles that are suitable for this;
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take heed that the veins are apparent as they descend upon their head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he feels the prickings in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the gullet or near the ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descensions are upon his feet, he feels it or pricks and has painful sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary to hold the needle in his right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and he holds all his hand lightly, and feels the prick in none of these places that we have said, until he comes to the empty space;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and it is the form of the ankle:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix one against another ankle, or the third where you have mastery, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then hold them evenly in moving one way and the other, to make them issue, and let the ankles be held by them, as it is their form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then anoint the joint with some of its own oil, and bind it in that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if it remains a bit, set this anvil or higher up, and make it so that it all issues forth.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back by straightening.
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so it is necessary that you envelop it with a bandage, so that it becomes whole.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then put the cup on the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus it is necessary that you do the same with the other hand, and in this way.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the head of the child is large and it is twisted at birth, or it has an assembled crooked head,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	then it is necessary that you put the spinal instrument between your two, and make the head straight and extract the crookedness;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	where you round it with the instrument called "almidach", which is shaped to come with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus in this way, you make the children have a natural large head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat the bones as fasteners,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps forward and it is held by the forceps, so it be bent, until the moisture that is or issues forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot issue, then cut into pieces at the muscles where you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce as much as the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he stands on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the administration at the mouth of the marrow is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if he is twisted in the belly or in the breast, it is necessary that you stretch him out with a wrapped cloth around the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and touch the belly or the breast, as much as the moisture that is there corrects.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are stretched out, and the head remains.
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	Here is the translation:
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then he applies a poultice or an onion, and makes a dressing for the wound;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the marrow is constricted by a hot abscess that has come there, then it does not need to be operated on;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then one must administer moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply poultices, and use soft, mollifying, and moistening remedies.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, thus amending what we have said about the living infant;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and so that one cannot operate, if one draws out the fragments, and does not leave anything of the secondary wound.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, amend what we have said about abscesses that come in the marrow;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if blood flows out, put it into a warm bath, and amend other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had swallowed an infant that had been dead, then she conceived another on top of it, and the other was dead too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, he came to have abscesses in his belly, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to greatly suppurate.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong poultice, and there came out a bone, and after some days others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel greatly, because for this reason the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I touched the wound and extracted many bones, until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman soon felt a little better, and then coughed up a piece of bone from her body;

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the hip back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the presser, where one examines the books; and at .ij. turnings as .ij. heads of the .ij. ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle from the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood;

et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the midst of the instruments should be two adjustments of this same box, which are fastened on one side and the other, half a palm's length or a little more;

et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has two heads, two joints, as you see, of a palm's length, and two fingers wide;

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	Here is the translation:
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in childhood, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his arm, and then make him stretch out his condition, and hold your hands at the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and let him breathe through that, it is good.

toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cut or put in water on the fire; then place a cane or tube under the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the patient,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let the blistering occur as long as the vapors come from the marrow; then it will become sterile, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary inflammation happens quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not become feverish, then instruct the patient to soak their left hand in oil of sesame or in a poultice of alta, and then apply the remedy naturally.

mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must move gently to the right and to the left, and then draw back; if it comes and dislocates again.

si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	Here is the translation:

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation perceived, thus it has been subtly obscured.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are nodulation, and those that come from beneath the foundation of the furrow, or in the space of the two parties,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and in the meantime moisture accumulates white or subtle swelling,

des emorroydes	of the hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are in two kinds of manners: either they are deep inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they suddenly burst forth with blood,

et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them at your fingers, then touch, and sprinkle above some warm powders that are in the fire of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then heal with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot be opened, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and bitter clusters to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can open freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patients take hold, and their veins are outside the foundation, then it is a light treatment;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you prick them with your finger or nails, and cut, then heal as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you make the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too large; and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one there to correct the excessive flow of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a dressing of milky oil or rose oil or cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest until it heals, and when they are healed, if they receive treatment of ointment and other treatments, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	you should cleanse the wounds or basis
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is cleansing of wounds in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no value.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you raise to the point of a spatula or on one nail the scab which does not allow it to moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then the treatment as long as it is swollen thus as it is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be treated, then recommence the rubbing more strongly than before, as long as it hurts a lot, and becomes scarred;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment as long as it is healthy.
dou fremit	because of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A blister is a small faulty appearance against the body, and goes very much deep inside;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the frost, and one feels it as if dead from cold, and it comes into all of the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread of a bird's feather, or a strong thread from a wild duck, and put that thread on the frost, so that the circles thoroughly encircle the frost all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all along the thread so that you encircle all around the frost, and put it deep inside, and tear out the frost from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cane of iron or copper in this form, and be subtle underneath and straight above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, for you must hold at the finger, and press; And if you see, cauterize the fremited place, as it is before or in front of the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or of molten iron or steel; and never make these small and large instruments, according to the ones that are prepared for them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Here is the translation:
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large cluster is above width, where the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived from within; and it has a perforation on one of the sides, .ij., and on the other, .i.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be where one puts the medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and let it be perceived all around with many small perforations,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and let there be between each perforation .i. a space of an inch, then put in these perforations .i. strong thread made from twisted thread, twisted in .x. or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if one takes the thread in front of a strong wire, then cauterize; and that's the form of a circle ring.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the cauterized area with oil or egg whites, or similar things, then apply it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister presses with his two hands together, so that it be completely visible, then extract the cauterized area, and lift the patient's legs to the partition.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to issue forth, let it flow as much as it can; and if it sleeps one night completely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him for a disease of bowel decay, and the medicine hastens to issue, then recommend it as long as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or an abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the form of the subtle enema on whom the skin is held back:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments by hand and by medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they were made, and according to the locations or where the wounds were made, and of what they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds were made are by thrust of stone, and cut of sword and of dagger, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or of similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which were made according to the locations of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory comes back to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it's a matter of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the aposteme's heat: if you make it healthier on the cephalic side at once, even if there is little blood from the wound, and let the healing be opposite to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from repletion of wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let his food be diminished, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply to the wound, where abscesses are coming, a cotton cloth soaked in rose oil or wine steeped in it;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess forming, apply to the wound, so it is fresh and whole with its blood, and not moved by air or powder, which I will discuss a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound is moved, apply to it some ointments, so that it may be healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by tugging, if they are assembled by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and it stinks, and holds on only to a little, if it suppurates; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard skin in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as broths and roasted meats, also as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find decayed skin or rotten flesh, and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut out all the rot, and throw it away, then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if he has wounded in the wound or vein, which without delay, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, so you should tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit him, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which soothes thus that the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense, one part; dragon's blood, two parts; living chalk, three parts, and powder subtly.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill in the wound, and hold it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, so it does not swell; for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one make a poultice of hot chalk alone, when one has not heated the blood of dragon, but rather that the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has moved the wound, meanwhile in this state, then do not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply to some digested ointments, or poultices made of wheat flour and honey, so that it pours forth well;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of other treatments until they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the breakage of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes to the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not to put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be soothing, as you heat it in gentle water, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it also in gentle water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other mines of a similar kind, and apply moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, prick or pierce at a lower level;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then it dries up, and heals, and the cautery skill is a profession;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the arteries, and the conducts are guarded, through which the food goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the artery on the vein of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then strain it strongly, and leave it some days, then cure the wounds of excess flesh as much as it is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if it has broken bones, if you treat them as you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound ripens;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be drained and aligned with the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or of knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow of lance or of knife, and the wound is very deep, then consider whether the wound has become putrid, as soon as the patient complains: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not stop the bleeding.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and look at the body, and observe the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and apply it several times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, put much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound several days, two, three, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil tremor of heart, nor signs of bad alignment;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, if you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with tents and other treatments, until they are healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and it is an ulceration, then you know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one must do it.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, of cauterization; and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has taken hold of pieces, so that the wound heals, and the badly set bones are reset.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not reset, let the wound putrefy, so that it lightens the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds as other limbs are the judgments, as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	for the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and middling and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes the intestine, or the veins of the intestines, because of the internal obstruction;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more troublesome, and sometimes it is better to have a small wound than a large one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one has to reset the intestines in place, so that they are not displaced from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestine swells as soon as it feels cold, if it returns to points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this it is necessary to treat the affected area, for that reason one must reposition the intestine to its place like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common injuries occur in the injury of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the injury of other wounds of the body and four other proper injuries are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are more prone with the stitching of the belly, and I will describe one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine is outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and grievous thing is to restore it, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or by the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	where because the intestine is weakened by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is chilled, warm it in some manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or a bundle of cloth in hot water, then apply it gently,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you cook in hot water squatting and cypress and spike,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the swelling goes down;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and often do these restraining winds, and it is wonderful that we relieve the soul by reducing the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling go away, moisten the intestine with water or wine and evil humors are cured,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for it is aligned with the entry of a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound at the instrument where one gathers the blood vessels;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to remove what is excessive in the cutting,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut unless there is great need for it;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for making an incision:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curve and do not dig too deeply, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back in place according to its natural form in its own proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	look at it with care, for that is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is on the lower part beneath the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you lay the patient on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and it is in the lower part beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	Put the tip of the cautery iron higher than the surrounding areas,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the injured parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you place them in a way that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say for great wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds heal when they are well-dressed,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then you hold them in your hands, I mean a pitiful minister who pulls out the entire bandage with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and brings together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is the common way of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound, I do not spare, and I fix a needle or it has a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the skin with the skin of the siphos,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the eleven chief veins which are swollen;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain with a double thread within the needle of the said vein,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the eleven heads of the wound in a convenient way,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let the tenth finger of space, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then you thread the cord just as you did the first needle
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing so according to what you have mastered of the needles
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and coarse
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for it is necessary that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and open up the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the heads of the veins, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold taut or wrap around the heads of the veins to keep them steady,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of cutting the veins is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because he suffers from a needle or .ij.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second injury is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather the .ij. heads of skin and the .ij. heads of soft flesh together at a needle or where it has a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you reset the needle to the part where you started, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch suits the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that one had in the belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a lancet
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and it was a wound more than a palm in size,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was well into the intestines, about two palms of size,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and it was a wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I restore the intestine then when it has been still 23 hours, for
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn shut just until 15 days, and it was cured, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him with ointment, for I stood in a place where one found no medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a gentle pressure more on the wound cotton very often in a day, and the washing of water and honey until it was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and sew up the part that is torn just to the depth within;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the skin straight on, if you have sewn up the head of the siphaeus or the stitching or where you have sewn with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and have them pierce another part of the inner section just up to the outer layer;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this treatment is that you sew as the furrier makes the skins,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and let one side of it dry for a while, and then take it up again, until the treatment is completely accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of treatment, which Galen properly describes,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If it is so, like a fountain, which naturally assembles the damaged parts together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one head to another head, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix a needle or head of a probe near the affected limb, and make it pierce only the area that is swollen.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the damaged heads of the joint be restored.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce the weak part just up to the depth within.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as it clears the syrupy thick liquid;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make them pierce one and the other of the weak part just up to the depth within, in the other thick liquid of the mirach that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the mother manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says this passage, and no one bears witness to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must cauterize the belly with three needles, or have a thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is the wound most grievous than the other wounds of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus showing that the art has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you reset the intestine and the gut; then put on the powder of irritating charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if he has moved his arm, put it back into its proper joint, as long as the wound is swollen;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the phlegm, and be careful of the skin, and the membrane;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicines, put them on, as soon as the wound begins to fester, abundantly;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and let him move his arm often during the day so it may be healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicine in many conditions since the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you apply a light ointment of tempered heat, or in an ointment of rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put them between the fingers, and beneath the soles;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or pruritus in the belly, and often it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they give a cluster of red wine tepidly, and meanwhile the pruritus reaches just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and they perceive it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "hungry" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the weakness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approximation of its natural tendencies.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound's crust falls off, set it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned towards black or green, then you must lie down the black humour that comes from the blood, which descends into it;
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the joints in place during the procedure below the wound until it is ready to be aligned, as the nerves and veins are freed, and the wound is prepared.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is swollen, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced in the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and was swollen and became fistulous, and thus he felt nausea and windiness;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a treatment according to what I could do, and did not stop subtling until he was healthy, and the limbs were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sound, I doubted that the patient had a bad humor in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they say that certain experimenters claim that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied off in some manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm grips on large wounds, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the grip has opened the mouth, then place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it stretches its mouth thus;
