et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts off the head, and it holds still so that it cannot dislocate.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another foment on afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head sticks in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread that should be much loosened,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie it to the head of this thread, i.e., a subtle twisted thread of flax,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then thread the filament into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its proper place.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching wounds is not done except according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, so there is no ingenious way to heal it, except with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it swells up, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is hairy and renders a bud.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the vertebra's hard, rough, and white nodulation, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in a clear burn, and sometimes dense;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and sometimes little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not clean, and there is no flesh;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the small passage of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or through its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not let bad flesh grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the lesion is putrid, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where the property in the region is slow in digestion, and slow in health, and weak by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by hand operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula has in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come to the big veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the spleen, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in one of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it reaches the property of the principal member, and similar to them.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if it happens that there is no fistula that does not approach exactly to the place I have told, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you examine it, if you take a straight rod of iron or steel, the fistula is straight, if it is so;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a subtle probe of lead;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the hairs grow flat within the twistedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and you should make a fistula with perforated hands and you cannot search it well by feeling,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you touch it with one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one perforation to another, and it becomes cloudy;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then you should examine your power to know if it has bone or nerve, and is covered in the front.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and burn for the putrid matter and the corrupted flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, then you should cut through deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply gentle medications for the ague, and the poultices just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess which is remained at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts ointments on the healthy flesh, so that it be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy by this, then cautery it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or principal nerves are not causing you grief or harm, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, so let the ruler remove as much of the decay as possible;
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the things that are wounded as much as it can be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and return to the beginning as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	You know that you are not able to move just then:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it reveals itself and you ask as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If you do not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tourniquets,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with an instrument suitable for this,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if he has many bones, if they are all extracted, do not leave a single one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you cut and moisten and flesh, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot dislodge them within an hour, then place on the wound a poultice that induces rotting,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let them be so that the yellowness is around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have less difficulty with the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as a thigh or a shin,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove so much of the corrupted matter that the blackness is entirely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the decayed corpse, and it reaches close to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to clean and cover everything up to the corrupted area, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you prepare an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	It was a young man of twenty years old, who had pain in his leg for a reason that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the humors went to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to remove the cause by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctor, in their foolishness, opened so widely that the abscesses opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they run much of matters, and become fistula, and they come much of perforations that all glide smoothly and moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mirror mirrored cure within these years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those that run through the perforations to a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young boy becomes red, and has a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I thrust a tent into one of these pores, and then sought out all the pores,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against others from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the pores as much as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and he found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came just up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me from the corrupted bone, and I believed there was no other corruption, except for that which I stopped;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines, applying them gently for a long time, and could not soothe;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as it was before;
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continued corruption in the bone, and the swelling, and then the ostosis, and I thought to reunite the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do more than cupping on a palm of the bone, and the traitor flees all his moisture,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was quickly healed and relieved soon after,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not need to recommence the work for a long time because of the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the evacuation of blood is often unsuccessful, but it was completely healthy,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard crust formed on the wound, and it was of good disposition and had no hindrance or contradiction at all, neither in going nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be soothed in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Here is the translation:
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to stretch up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another ligature on the larger vein, and tie it above the skin which is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stop the blood flow, so that you extract the corrupt skin from below,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin above the joint where you saw the swelling, so that the swelling does not affect the skin;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a bandage beneath the bone for protecting the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to sew as one can see and feel the corruption, and to sew again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if the flesh is entirely uncovered; then put a splint beneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then let it be from one part to the other the corruption, and let the sewer of the length of the corruption be few, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and let the bone or it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut off;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is on the finger of the hand, or on the toe of the foot, it is very strongly attached;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and examine it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve contradict you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the nerves for coping with these bones are many, according to the alignment of the bones and the appearance of the joints,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare each similar instrument of operation;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the methods for diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument you will need, according to what it requires.
dou feu	for fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head bursts out either because of denseness or because of fervor;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corrosion through the treatment of medicines, and it does not improve at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should couple that member up to the place or where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by means of death, or through spite, which is greater, than the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards there is numbness after the blackening, then it spreads to corrosion of limb after limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and it takes over the whole body; if you hasten to amputate,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the finger's tip, thus the blame, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, thus the blame at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, thus the blame at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there are no better remedies than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all this is done when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then it seizes after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, it seizes the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then it seizes at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of copper or of sewing the limb is such that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister on one of the lower ligaments, and another minister on the other upper ligament,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dissect the flesh that is between the two ligaments to a spacious width, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then place a dressing or bandage, and put a linen cloth on each part, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy skin,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and let it come to the patient for another wound and abscess healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if a flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the skin hastily,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some retaining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then let the numb member recover with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will count it as if he had a wound in his own foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a black spot that seemed to be burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first into his toe on his foot, so much that it took over the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man sees the corrosion, if he hastens to cover the foot, and it was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corrosion returned on the hand, or on the arm, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied things that rebounded after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corroisons;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it seemed to me that I covered the hand, and I did not want, that I had hope of rebounding the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and fear also that he may cut off his hand, so it does not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the veins of the man were weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to amputate his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not seen it happen except for the fact that one does something else, so one has mastery over it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Here is the translation:
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they roar and burst, and the belly swells, and their eyes become dim, just like some vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is as subtle as a thin piece of cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not run to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such an illness is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it comes just to the bone in the foreground, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if it is that you take off all around, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a thin layer;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not be mistaken because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the skin is wounded, and the corruption is not in the foreground,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, if the treatment of the clyster thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look at the sins are large, and the flux that comes from it is of foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then the clysterization of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take sage, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put skin in the vessel at the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	as long as the medicine is red, and it thickens like honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from that according to your need, and make it into water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the wound, and hold back the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay there for two hours, then extract it by sprinkling;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times, until the breast is swollen, and the pus is released.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and it is never clarified with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not available, and it is that you take ashes from the wood of a vine, and throw water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain, and clarify, until you know that the breast is well swollen;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither Egyptian medicine nor ash of cinders
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if they are treated with a mixture of water and honey or if they have a little bit of litharge in powder;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you treat it with a mixture of honey and wine, which has the properties of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the senses are well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you clarify what makes the flesh grow in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you clarify some medicines and ointments, whose properties or treatments of the ointments I have mentioned;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the pierced skin of the back is small, and the vein of the cluster cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you widen a little with an iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian stitching,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or royal stitching, so that it may be widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then sew and leave it slightly loose, so that the cluster or the vein can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if they pierce where the swelling is above, so apply the cupping or lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the swelling is in the front, then do not let it be pushed back;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cup the underlying seat thus as you have seen,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it appears in such a way that the swelling runs to the lowest place where it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the belly is perforated, if they do not let it swell there
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the seat of the womb below as you saw,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	it appears in such a manner: that the belly collapses lightly downwards, and does not leave anything of the belly;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the womb,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stand above the drapery of the loincloth that covers the whole breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then grasp with force at the spot of the nipple of the breast, a little larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then there is a gentle pressure above on the other drapery according to the quantity of the nipple,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it above the nipple of the breast to align the bow, and do not remove the large drapery unless after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the perforated breast, often opens by opening the cavity,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know that which runs from the cavity, whether it is venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed of the patient's feelings of pain or name, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps above the perforated breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that the senses are hurt already, and approach the saints;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then disentangle it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you disentangle the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change to another dressing, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the senses throw away indigestible matter after many days, know that the senses are not hurt.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if you come subtly to a long tension, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the health approaches. For it is men who slow down the healing of their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the bowel indigests itself for many days after much work, know that the senses are not troubled;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the senses slow down to understand, and it is delayed, then apply medicines which are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	If one's treatment is defective, because it has a large part of glass, and it's the last resort medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take defective treatment, and make it with rose oil, and the extract of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and this same mixture makes honey cooked into a thick paste,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defective treatments are not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take mirre and aloe and incense, and the broth, and dust on honey when it is above the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then in glueing, I drag, and it sticks to the breast, and often an Aristologist administers for a long time,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of veins and a hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the treatment is prolonged, and it is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is in depth, and makes an impression on the bone, or the hard members, or the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A boil is an abscess that grows beneath the nail of the thumb.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, or by chance it grows on other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if it comes to an abscess of the sole,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and corrodes and gnaws away until it corrodes the root of the nail, and by chance it corrodes the whole thing;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come the ulcers up to the bone, as far as they bring putrid pain, and the head of the finger is swollen and large, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut to the fair flesh, removing all the superfluity which is more than the ankle,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh in, and it begins to prick, and the blister,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put the straight edge underneath the nail that does not touch the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the end above, and cut subtly and lightly into the flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh of the wound burning and corroding medicines to expel everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wounds thoroughly until they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut around it, and remove the decayed part, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the decayed part corrupting, cut around it in this way, just as it was said before;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal him until he is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is feverish, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then it is necessary to heal him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the finger at the joint of the thumb, cutting across above;
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cut does not go too close to the flesh which is beneath the finger, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something soothing on it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that swoops down from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two fingers that are born in the hands of certain men by chance are all numb,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance it has a piece or bone, and never an nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them grow at the root of the joint, where growth is in no way from the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow on no knuckle of the toe do not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that grow at the joint of the toe, perhaps move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of one who is wounded is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: if you hold it too tightly, you cooperate.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In he who is born or should be in the rear, it is necessary that you cut around the round flesh just up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone to a suitable size for that, then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that come together come from birth, or from sudden injury, or from fire burn, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cope with this pain, if the finger must be repaired according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moistened drapes in rose oil, so they do not become painful.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of subtle plaster, so that the wounds are joined, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Here is the translation:
Des vils	Bad humors
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are bad veins full of superfluous melancholic fluids that come from many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they have more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you apply no further purging of the colon, and then the healthy regime of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is according to seven methods: one is that they cut, and they draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another method is that you open a vein, and draw out all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The surgical strike is according to this method: raise the first leg of hot water very strongly, so that the gross blood is subtly separated,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient down from the thigh just to the part beneath the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cauterize the vein in the left arm, or in the right arm, or in the third arm, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then bleed and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one vein to the other, until as much blood as the virtue of the patient can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then lay it down, and instruct him to abstain from eating black bile-inducing foods;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommend the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	Here is the translation:
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and the swollen leg becomes red and hot, and inflates the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat him with fire, and then cover the vein from the loin to the knee joint, or in the part below the thigh;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scrape the vein of each part, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters under the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then apply the rule beneath, so that it is elevated from the skin, and then attach it to the onion's handle.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then shape it in another way, thus two inches; then strip the skin from the vein so that it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then lift it to the root, as you have done, and attach it to another uncle, as you had done previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then shape another size, or more if you have mastery of it, then lift it, and shape it to the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then burn with fire up to the second joint; then strip of joint in joint, as far as it goes entirely into fury, then the scab.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot burn and raise, if you insert a needle everywhere, with a strong double thread.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and burn and raise, and insert beneath, with a straight needle, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it goes in;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not suppurate, for if it suppurates, you cannot burn or raise, and it comes to harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have treated it all, put on the place of the wound a molten lead in wine and rose oil; and heal until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the veins are contracted and twisted and enveloped together, and they are not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary to bend them gently, but do not cut them off; and treat them as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron instrument with which one cuts the veins is curved, and does not cut too deeply, so that it does not cut into the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of thick curvature, for if it was subtle, it would seize the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs nor trees, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it grows another part besides the legs, and this comes from the putrid matter that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes within the body of snakes and worms, you will find between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes its location, and begins the vein to issue forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, it is necessary that you envelop with a piece of cloth around one and a half inches up to the nail, and the knee.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the poultice be on the leg, and every time it is not on the defect, if the envelop wraps around the poultice, and the tumor;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut into its root, until it is entirely separate;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut into it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putridity or pus, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of this, it is necessary that it be treated little by little just to the head, and nothing remains or decays;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is sometimes this vein when it is treated with five points of a hand, or ten.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a vein comes to me, from which it issues from ten points of a hand's length, and when you cut it, if you find a bone or pierced place, and pierce it just to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if all of it issues; and let the material that is within be evacuated, and apply to the wound medicines which induce purging without any delay, then cure it as with abscesses.
