Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of veins that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "ox disease", because it often affects the oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small vein that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he will feel well along the alignment of limb by limb, as long as they straighten the skin or it heals, and thus be cured;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by bad digestion of certain humors, if they come forth as worms and snakes and lice and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt not of its evil, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it returns, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to cure and treat, if one cannot force it except when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then it is necessary that you bind the limb above and below with a strong and tightly wrapped bandage,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and the arm is strong, and if the vein is deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does, if it runs to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, hold the eyebrow firmly, then press on it, and pull it back;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is suitable to use the patient's purification of the body with medicines that dissolve bad humor pores,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of rotten meat causing putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered a swollen arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and afterwards, he will soon raise his eyes as if to a shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more stiff than anything, as if living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that place, and fixes itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little afterwards it ran throughout the whole body, until it came into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then I account for her who turns inward towards the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen that many had wanted to move the pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had not seen it, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, it seemed that her windiness was constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it didn't appear to me according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and reopened veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, it appears thus as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If you hold above and below firmly, and then press on it as much as that swelling constrains the blood flow there;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those who burst the swellings, as if foul pills, and serpent's pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they settle.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and notched, and hollowed out.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have sharp angles, and of those which have lengths, and of those in which there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which settles in no member settles according to sharp ways: either in a principal member it notches,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	As brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls into a bad state of these organs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is fitting that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrowhead is in the head and pierces the bone, and the swelling falls which is on the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	it is when there are symptoms of scotoma and numbness and vertigo in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and permutation of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes it is without strength in the nostrils, or in the ears; and sometimes it affects speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and falls from the white moist wound resembling a poultice, and also falls out as if bruised flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, you will know of the treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls or pierces, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not loose.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves as if it were a poultice, and brings forth black blood, and produces coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you will know without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow wound that does not swell the forearm is that without excessive swelling from the wound, and the throat becomes inflamed, and the patient's complexion changes, and breathes deeply and quiets the cold arthritis.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow head remains in the covering of the thigh, it is beneath the small ribs; and it causes great anguish and great pain and breathing; and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow head remains in the stomach, perhaps it jumps from the wound some undigested food matter.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow head remains in the belly, and it does not pass a point of feces through the intestine, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead remains in the bladder, and the urine jumps up and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the arm and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the forearm and the elbow and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrowhead is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, I will tell you what happened to me, because that is why you do something similar.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man whose arrowhead fell or was stuck in the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I touched it, and I pulled from another part beneath the fat of the ear, and it was suddenly healthy without treatment.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrowhead that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the papery skin,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrowhead was embedded, and I could not touch it except for the point towards the hollow,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and it was a large arrowhead from a Turkish bow, with an entire iron shaft without any ornaments; the game was healthy, and no bad accidents happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And one takes out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arabian arrow at the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I softened the barbs, and I made them subtle as much as I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man's body, which was stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when it had passed thirty days, he did not move at all from his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and I extracted it, and I treated the wound forcefully, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow fell out or down, and the wound was sewn over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained within him, and it did not change its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did I find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And he saw another man whose arrow had fallen on his face, and the wound was swollen.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he suffered great pain from it; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And they extracted an arrow from the king's prince's nose, which had stuck in his brain,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly leaning to the right side; and the entire arrow was deeply embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the cure after it had fallen for three days. If I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought to touch it with a subtle finger, and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a piercing pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the patient a well-plastered digestive tract, because the intestines are not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and it appears to me that the intestines are of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster daily, and resolve the wound again, and thus the patient remains for a long time in good health.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow, that is, a day within his nose; and it was told to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the medicine to the wound with a corrosive hand, as long as it was uncovered.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I touched, and felt the head of the arrow which had stuck into the flesh;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I probed into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, so much that the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it crossed well into the limits within three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then scarify if the wound is that I would touch the tendons, and the muscle on one side and the other, and cannot issue;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to subtily and ingeniously make maneuvers of strumments, until I took them for well-made tendons.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I may extract it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror shows that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you about the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you set your treatment on those things which I do not say, for the book cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compare well a little great thing, and on those things which are present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here is the translation:
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed except according to seven manners.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the soil or they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps forth where it enters, it's an arrow entering into the flesh, and it does not jump forth at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is porous within, and let the issue be cleared.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot exit, then leave it thus for some days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, then pierce all around with a subtle iron, so that the eyes around are enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just up to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient: if you do not extract it, but leave it thus until it is even after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for the vein approaches just to the skin, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the vein is not fixed in the bone, and does not approach just to the skin,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains some days without bad accident, if the engine of the draw works.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed in this way and cannot issue forth, then administer tareres around, as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is pushed back into its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, if one desires to remove it entirely;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if you draw it out with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or vein, if it is so placed that the wound may be large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw back the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow where it holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If you remove the skin which is implanted with .ij. parts through the muscles that you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the wings of the arrow, so that you can extract it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly be careful not to break the arrow, so that you extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it remain until the swelling has subsided, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if you find that blood is flowing contrary to what we have said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising near a nerve and vein, and do not attempt to move the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether it is twisted or straight, or firmly or loosely; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow fell on them;
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that it can be, and if you cannot, then place it according to what the signs show you;
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens into something of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it by touch.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then upon it, so that the tongs can grasp, and then extract it: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot exit, leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if he suffers from the arrow wound, it is, he should apply the poultice to the entire wound;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the wound is deep, and you want to administer a poultice, if he administers it, it will hide the instrument;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then apply force;
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is hairy, he should apply the instrument with a pointed end, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the veins are, so you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as it covers.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the foot or thigh or belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut above, so you cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, so that is the task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of them: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the cutting beak is also like a bird's claw,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For applying heat to the tip of the arrow, as it is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for applying heat and for extracting if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one bleeds are 21, because it has or is the head 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	it is to know: there are two bones behind the ears, which are called the "herbech" twain;
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the eyelids of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the small wounds that are on the column;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the small veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the small veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is the left side of the head, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the vein called "faste" is composed of the cephalic and the basilic,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the hollow,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that one bleeds, which appears manifestly on the skin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little vein is the one that is between the thumb and the finger, and if it rains on them;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the feet are, there are three veins: one is beneath the curve of the left thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right thigh; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other leg are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient catharrhes, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the healthy one, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are of a rough fabric; then strain the patient's neck to a view,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	as long as the eyes appear behind the ears in the eyes depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the humps touch your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of an inch;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it beneath the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein above,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and open the skin and the vein well, you must make two traverses, and let out as much blood as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold steady and raise it, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is worth migrating to an ancient one,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swollen, and accustomed optometry, and with the course of the watery eyes;

et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches out his neck, so that the .ij. veins appear openly;

puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then raise the heart to the vein above your finger's tip, and put the lancet beneath,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and raise the vein high, and the cupping glass, just as you have done with other veins, and make correction of blood according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then anoint the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form the scar, and let it be until it is healthy; and we have already spoken of their cupping and their extraction, where the beginning of the book commences.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the health of the cephalic veins, as for ancient facial diseases, and for migraine, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and it is of such quality that the patient strains his neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and hold the vein until it is healthy and never again swells up with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Here is the translation:
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting no ligament, as before;

And if the veins are subtle, perhaps they break; then make correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery over it, and then place it on the cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The veins of the vein that you take from the ague, and from severe pain, and from facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Here is the translation:
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the health is such that the patient holds his neck, then he holds his nose with his left hand.

car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now start to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let too much blood flow in, and make the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, because it is almost completely restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and it's the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The wisdom of the twelve guides helps in the strengthening of the vein, and at the beginning of meselry, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and similar things;

puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then redo another part in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and hold the veins moderately;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it just until morning, so that the wound may be healthy.
De la sainie des leivres	About the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The wisdom of the veins above the lips is recognized by a hole in the mouth, and by decay of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and painful nose and interior.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the wisdom is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck steady as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left;

cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Here is the translation:

De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healthiness below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healthiness of the veins that are below the tongue helps afterwards the healthiness of the head, and it's at the narrowing of the throat, and in the diseases of the eye, and in the diseases of the mouth;

saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Here is the translation:
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of fire cautery, which are commonly used, are healthy according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where they prick everywhere, it is called "flaime" widely, or subtle olive oil if they cut deeply, and it is called "anesil";

Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the "flaime" widely known, is very renowned, and is wide as you see:

et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for cleansing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cleansing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the feet, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to proceed carefully, and he must beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he touches the artery, and a stream of blood comes out, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not be pricking the flame, but cutting so as to make a scar.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the abscess does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you extract it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	where you feel no pain of it, or you touch on the vein in the arm: it appears manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the scab on the flame anesthetized, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the condition of the vein, then it is necessary that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the vein as much as you can feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the vein of the wound, and then stretch out the arm, and cover the vein with a flame anesthetized;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the limb swollen, for it is of the artery: avoid this then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swelling upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is without an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hasten thou then, and put thy finger on for a long time, then remove thy finger if the blood is stagnant, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	let the arm be still, and let it thus, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move them until they are healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stanched, and it vanishes, and the medicines are not present, then cut the artery so it opens, for the head of the veins; and stanch the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of flesh from the fistula, and make it fat, and take one of the embers and lay it well just next to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is stanched, that's good; if not, then apply a remedy, as we have said, of powders that stanch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stanched wounds are not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the possession of the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	Here is the translation:
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that lies beneath, and if he presses too hard, and he touches the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it becomes inflamed and the veins are irritated, and by chance they cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, then it is necessary that you sharpen the instrument anew; and avoid touching the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the fingers, thus they make it two inches long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the head helps, which draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed at the flame olive or at the flame martian, for it is the safest of all the veins, since it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must seek the lightest vein, and not grievously harm oneself when one first starts, and recommences;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance inflame the eyes of some men, when one fails at first, but it does not grievously harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not diminished for fear of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bloodletting be done on one of the three veins that are near the elbow: namely, the cephalic, the fasting, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bloodlet in the beginning of spring, and in autumn, and in winter after menstruation, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bloodlet on the first day or the third, after 8 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered for the illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but rather it depends on whether the need is by day or by night, at all hours and in all tenseness.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not suitable to cauterize children until 13 years old, nor a woman carrying a fetus less than four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should they cauterize the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be cauterized, in whatever manner it may be, then it is necessary that they evacuate the intestines of a lighter cluster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has much bad flatulence retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful humors from the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One does not heal quickly who is too full of meat, nor one who is drunk, as long as he is feverish, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and it is worse to be on the way to health after a passion of colic, and vomiting, and decay of stomach, and multiple conception by a woman, and labor, watching and fasting, and all that takes away virtue, or because of the arm or doucors body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then refine the humors, if the blood is thick, by meat and by drinks and by medications, if you have a lot of power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter into a bath, where nothing does him harm, to refine the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and you bleed from the vein above the third rib, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and beware of that day's work, and of puncture, and of luxation, and of similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be gentle and joyful, and let the vein be higher than the one from which you bleed, and rub the arm twice or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then extract the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the vein;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the shoulder with the hands until the veins swell, and feel it;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then anoint the sinew with a little oil of a small amount, then place his finger of his left hand on that vein beneath the shoulder a little where it wants to heal;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not flee and fails to be pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee as if cords from the sinew, and if they have such ones that are full of windiness;
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Here is the translation:
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, it is the wound that is too constricted, because it is necessary that the surgeons be skilled in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, then recommence a little below that place or on the side, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are inflamed, and the patient is in a spasm, leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps he will come to abscesses suddenly; do not enter or bathe, then recommence the treatment as it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the perforation is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it does not issue as much blood as you see, then make a hole in the same spot with the entire flame straightaway;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and hold the egg a little hastily, so that the eyes are inflamed; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the eye inflamed, do not recommence the bleeding, and put a little oil of olives on it, for it alleviates the body's pain of blood, and is mixed in this vein the oil that is there;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and then administer the oil of olives in each bleeding wound that you bleed the veins, to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same mixture makes a triangular and bulging shape when one places it on the limb; if one subtly senses the vein and separates it when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not healthy except at the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and place on the limb a moist sponge in water and in a little warm heat, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for some days without any blackness or greenness, it will not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put among some things of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calendula, master, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: put your hand on it, and if you find the soft spot at the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for it may happen in court without an artery; but the physician makes a plaster to harden the spot, then cures with another cure, until it be healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw each one's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because the patient's blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it thin out until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it suits the one who is full and strong, and has mastery of blood extraction, so that they do not make a larger wound, and the flames are large.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits them to bleed less often, and they should be bled in a slanting cut, not in a deep puncture.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of bleeding is free from decay of blood and from rupture of a nerve, and it is better than the bleeding that is done from afar rather than from near.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body fails at the health, it is necessary to give a mild poultice made from juice of green apples; if it is inflamed, then draw out three or four times the bad blood.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, then anoint before the health a mild poultice made from musky syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and well-fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it pains at the health, after the flow of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of beef, and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to anoint his arm, and heal another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great wound, that he anoints little by little, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to anoint his arm after the first healing, and it has a strong course, if he anoints seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to heal from another part, if he should anoint on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and it brings fever; if one wants to treat a great quantity, and enlarge the pores as much as it bursts into a sweat.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then you examine all the signs of health, and place your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come into his body.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens often, when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not matter when you see the arm dislocated, and make blood flow out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly on;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, he stretches the arm hastily, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be until it heals the second time; or you touch the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is congealed at the mouth of the vein issues forth.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put it on the small piece of silk, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to bleed the blood a second time, let it be in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of the healthiness is that the patient puts their hand in warm water, so that the fingers become red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then the healthiness now of the crossing, neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the openings be wide, and let it be healthy near the joint of the hand, and if you cannot issue from it, then put the hand in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not reinsert the hand into cold water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the health of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is no artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the little finger on the right hand is good for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put it in cold water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cross the vein, and if you cut it entirely, do not cause any grief;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not inject too much into the marrow, for the nerves are very close to the bare flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in warm water, if the wound is frozen, and cannot issue forth.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out as much blood as is necessary for the task, then put oil on the vein and sew it up quickly, and thus do for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the hand on the left side is good for the disease of the thigh, and do everything just as I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The health of the spleen is good for all the diseases that are below the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	like diseases of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its health is that the patients throw out their feet in warm water, and rub on the vein as long as it pierces.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and he must place it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go much in veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	strain there where the vein is larger or more open, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you strain above the foot, so beware of the nerves that are underneath, and the vein of traversing as in a coping; and let the flames be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the saneness cannot issue from it, then reset the foot in the water, and let the vein be well purged.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the sinews fail for the first time, start again from above a little, because the joints are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make a soporific of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The joints of the sciatic vein are at the gathering of strength, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is because of hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its sinew is that the patients are either in a bath or stretch above the gathering, and pull upwards with a third cord, two fingers twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you should try it in all ways that you can, and by crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is necessary that you touch it, for the veins are without sensation, and it is much responded to by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then feel for some vein that opens or gives a sign at the foot of the toe, and towards the little finger, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make a correction of the blood that you see, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healthy.
Des sainies de ventouse	The applications of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made of horns, or of brass, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that is without striking is done in two ways: either it is with full fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping that is done by striking and by extracting blood is done in 12 locations on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one of them is entirely asleep in the head; and the other is within the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and others on both sides of the neck; and the vein below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the vein of the shoulders; and the vein above the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the veins within the arms; and the veins of the legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the ventouses of the .ij. veins; and the ventousation does not draw blood, except from small scattered veins that are in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this one does not get accustomed to it, as one does when making a vein sound;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor at all by fire nor sense of fire, in any illness which comes from fullness, as long as the body is purged.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to evacuate, or by habituations, so we administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and meanwhile and in every tense;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they have the task of bloodletting, weigh heavily on the head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are some who experience a flow of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit out blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who sigh, and see nothing but blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to apply a poultice after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the nose is helped by the grease of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it does not seem that it should be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this poulticing is in the place of the health of the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not seem that he who is of cold complexion in use, or who has a catarrh, for this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of this it does not seem to me that the veins are used, nor those who have cold heads with bad diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often wounded, if they become obtuse, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of obtuseness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping on the neck is in place of the wounded head and the basilica, and therefore it is useful for the contraction of the foot.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to a fracture of the channel of the forearm, and to a bruise, and to a replenishment;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to puncture, for it holds too firmly, if there is obstruction of the liver or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds as it is called, affect the ribs on both sides if it hurts the head, and causes obtundation and migration, and constriction, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the vein of the basilica vein; and it is necessary that you instruct the surgeon to place his hand so he does not cut the artery, and does not see the return of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds below the chin affect the mouth disease, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the vein of the .ij. lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the back are worth an illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilations of the sides are worth as much as those of the veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon to not make too many perforations, for the tissue is full of flesh, and knows of veins and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the back is like emerods of deep foundation, and like diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of iron, so it has mastery to treat well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings of the legs feel openly, because they attract blood from all over the body, and are worth as ancient pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and recall the flowers; and are in the place of .ij. soporifics, and of .ij. chevilles, and altogether they enfeeble the body after long use, and bring about palsy in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping is that you put it on first empty, and suck at once, and put it on hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and feel the flow of blood; then firm, and reapply the cuppings, and take heed in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh, and clear pores: if it is necessary to pierce once softly, and make large wounds, and a little deeply; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is abundant, it is necessary to pierce .ij. times: the first time to subtly open the way for the abundant blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it must be cauterized a third time; and when we want to draw out a little blood by little, it suffices to hold it back only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we recommend doing it often; and if the blood is thick, we cauterize deeply, and the termination is that the coursing should be perceived suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who have obstructed pores, that you open the veins of oily and dissolutive apertures:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this way, with oil of violets, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in a glass, of oil of cress, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superficies are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it does not need to be treated with oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it needs to be washed after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or water of Morella, or water of Cucurbita, or water of Porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ajueil, or from the water of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have gross excesses rise from old wine, or from the water of brook, or from a decoction of anet or chamomile, or from other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not consider it healthier to apply a cupping glass before bathing, but rather after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep afterwards, following the cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary to warn when one should be cupped and when one has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are melancholic, and their blood is too agitated and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that they take cold things, such as apples, grapes, and lettuce in the shade, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and avoid pungent foods, and flesh of pork, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine moderately, which is between old and new, and avoid much, and avoid pungent foods and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be bled, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men triple or muscat before bleeding, or afterwards, to comfort the main limbs;
